<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- sensei: teacher, instructor
- kibun: feeling, mood
- omoidasu: to recall, to remember
- omoide: memories, recollections
- taichou: physical condition, state of health

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҲгҒҸгҒӘгҒЈгҒҹ (yokunaru): to become better [Past tense]
- гҒ§гӮӮ: even if (grammar pattern)
- гӮҸгӮӢгҒҸгҒҰ (warui): bad [Te-form]
- гҒҹгҒ№гӮүгӮҢгҒӘгҒӢгҒЈгҒҹ (taberu): to eat [Potential / Passive, Negative, Past tense]

TONE HINT:
- genkyou: present condition

Input: sensei donichi taicho yokunatta genki aru to гҒ§гӮӮ omoidasu memai ga kibun warukute taberarenakatta
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- genki: lively, full of spirit
- kudasai: please give me, please do for me
- genkyou: present condition
- hikidoki: good time to quit, right time to withdraw
- shoukou: lull, breathing spell

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гҒқгҒҶ: follow (grammar pattern)
- гҒҫгҒ’гӮҲгҒҶ (mageru): to bend [Volitional]
- гҒҷгӮӢ: the speaker humbly (does verb) (grammar pattern)
- гҒЁгҒҚ: when (grammar pattern)
- гҒӢгӮ“гҒҳгҒҫгҒҷ (kanjiru): to feel [Polite/Formal form]

TONE HINT:
- dousuruka: what would you do?

Input: konnichiha genki гҒқгҒҶ de naniyori soudesune tsuzuru wo hisan wo mageyou to гҒҷгӮӢ гҒЁгҒҚ ni kowabari wo kanjimasu ka
Output: /no_think
```

- yuukan: evening edition of a daily newspaper, evening paper

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҲгӮ“гҒ гӮҠ (yobu): to call out to [Such things as (tari)]
- гҒ“гҒЁ: (you) should (grammar pattern)
- гҒ§гҒҚгҒҫгҒӣгӮ“ (dekiru): to be able to do [Polite negative]

TONE HINT:
- dokusho: reading books

Input: shinbun wo yondari miru гҒ“гҒЁ shuuchuu dekimasen ka
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- shuuri: repair, mending
- jitsuyou: practical use, utility
- shuufuku: restoration, repair
- naosu: to repair, to mend
- shisutemu: system

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гҒҶгҒ”гҒ„гҒҹгӮҠ (ugoku): to move [Such things as (tari)]
- гҒҜ: as for / has (grammar pattern)
- гҒӢгӮҢгҒҫ (aru): to be [Potential, Polite/Formal form]
- гҒҠ: polite nominal and adjectival prefixes (grammar pattern)

TONE HINT:
- shitai: want to do

Input: hoka no hito ni ugoitari гҒҜ shitai no ga sokutei kitamuki aremasu hitokage mochikosu fukugen kumanaku mata ha sowasowa takusan гҒҠ toittemo tasukaru
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

#### LLM Output

> I want to move, but the cause is that the shadow of a person facing the opposite direction overlaps with the restoration, repair, system, and many other things, and even if I try, I cannot be saved.

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.

- kekka: result, consequence
- yasumi: rest, recess
- deshou: it seems, I think

```

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- korera: cholera
- oyako: parent and child
- okashii: funny, amusing
- kyoushi: teacher, instructor
- yukai: pleasant, delightful

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҸгҒӢгҒЈгҒҹ (wakaru): to understand [Past tense]
- гҒ„гҒҳгӮҮгҒҶ: so long as (grammar pattern)
- гӮҸгӮӢkгҒӘгҒ„ (warui): bad [Negative]

- hizuke: date

Input: wakatta sensei kore гҒ„гҒҳгӮҮгҒҶ warukunai ranai to iinokosu desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de happyoukai aru no de
Output: /no_think
```
